# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# OpenJDK JVM Bytecode Interpretation Loop

## Your Task

Find all C++ source files in openjdk/jdk that implement the JVM bytecode interpreter main dispatch loop: the bytecode dispatch table, the interpreter template generation, and the method entry point setup.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the domain domain.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/jdk--742e735d` (openjdk/jdk)

```json

}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

## Summary

The answer includes **48 C++ files** organized into three categories:

- `templateInterpreterGenerator_<arch>.cpp` - Code generation for each bytecode
- `templateTable_<arch>.cpp/hpp` - Platform-specific bytecode templates
- `interp_masm_<arch>.cpp` - Assembly macros for dispatch (with methods like `dispatch_base()`)
- `abstractInterpreter_<arch>.cpp` - Architecture specifics

- `set_entry_points_for_all_bytes()` for building dispatch tables

in:\\n\\n1. **src/hotspot/share/interpreter/templateInterpreter.hpp**: Defines the `DispatchTable` class which contains dispatch tables indexed by tosca (Top-Of-Stack CAche) state and bytecode value. Three dispatch tables are maintained: `_active_table` (currently used by interpreter), `_normal_table` (normal mode), and `_safept_table` (safepoint mode).\\n\\n2. **src/hotspot/share/interpreter/templateInterpreter.cpp**: Contains the actual dispatch table implementations and initialization of all three dispatch tables (`_active_table`, `_normal_table`, `_safept_table`) as well as wide instruction entry points (`_wentry_point`). Bytecode-by-bytecode interpreter loop\\n\\n## How the Dispatch Loop Works\\n\\nThe dispatch loop is executed in three phases:\\n\\n1. **Dispatch Table Population**: During JVM startup, `TemplateInterpreterGenerator::set_entry_points_for_all_bytes()` iterates through all bytecode values and calls `set_entry_points()` for each to build the dispatch tables. Each bytecode template generates platform-specific code and records its entry point.\\n\\n2. **Dispatch at Runtime**: The interpreter uses the appropriate dispatch table (`_active_table`, `_normal_table`, or `_safept_table`) based on execution mode. The bytecode value is loaded and used as an index into the dispatch table, providing the address of the handler code.\\n\\n3. **Dispatch Epilog**: After each bytecode executes, `dispatch_epilog()` or `dispatch_next()` functions load the next bytecode and repeat the dispatch process.\\n\\nEach architecture implements the core dispatch mechanism through its `interp_masm_*.cpp` file, which provides architecture-specific assembly macros like `dispatch_base()` that efficiently perform the table lookup and jump to the appropriate bytecode handler.\"\n}\n",

main dispatch loop in OpenJDK/JDK is implemented across multiple interconnected C++ files:\\n\\n## Bytecode Dispatch Table (Core Components)\\n\\nThe bytecode dispatch mechanism is centrally defined in:\\n\\n1. **src/hotspot/share/interpreter/templateInterpreter.hpp**: Defines the `DispatchTable` class which contains dispatch tables indexed by tosca (Top-Of-Stack CAche) state and bytecode value. Each entry is a 256-element table (one for each possible bytecode, since `length = 1 << BitsPerByte`). The `EntryPoint` class groups tosca-specific entry points into units. Three dispatch tables are maintained: `_active_table` (currently used by interpreter), `_normal_table` (normal mode), and `_safept_table` (safepoint mode).\\n\\n2. **src/hotspot/share/interpreter/templateInterpreter.cpp**: Contains the actual dispatch table implementations and initialization of all three dispatch tables (`_active_table`, `_normal_table`, `_safept_table`) as well as wide instruction entry points (`_wentry_point`). Also defines return entry points for various invoke bytecodes.\\n\\n## Interpreter Template Generation\\n\\nThe template-based code generation system is implemented in:\\n\\n1. **src/hotspot/share/interpreter/templateInterpreterGenerator.hpp**: Defines the `TemplateInterpreterGenerator` class which generates interpreter templates.\\n\\n2. **src/hotspot/share/interpreter/templateInterpreterGenerator.cpp**: Contains core template generation logic:\\n   - `generate_all()`: Main method that generates all interpreter templates\\n   - `set_entry_points_for_all_bytes()`: Populates dispatch table entries for all bytecodes\\n   - `set_entry_points(Bytecodes::Code code)`: Sets up entry points for a specific bytecode\\n   - `generate_and_dispatch()`: Handles bytecode code generation and dispatch\\n   - Various helper methods for counting bytecodes, tracing, and histogram generation\\n\\n3. **src/hotspot/share/interpreter/templateTable.hpp/cpp**: Defines the `Template` class which describes properties and code generators for each bytecode. Each bytecode has a corresponding template that specifies its behavior and how to generate its code.\\n\\n## Main Interpreter Initialization\\n\\n**src/hotspot/share/interpreter/interpreter.cpp**: Contains the main interpreter initialization functions:\\n- `interpreter_init_stub()`: Calls `Interpreter::initialize_stub()`\\n- `interpreter_init_code()`: Calls `Interpreter::initialize_code()`\\n- `InterpreterCodelet`: Represents a single interpreter code unit\\n- `CodeletMark`: Manages code generation for individual codelets\\n\\n## Architecture-Specific Implementations\\n\\nEach CPU architecture implements the bytecode dispatch mechanism with platform-specific optimizations:\\n\\n### X86/X86-64:\\n- **src/hotspot/cpu/x86/templateInterpreterGenerator_x86.cpp**: Base x86 interpreter generator\\n- **src/hotspot/cpu/x86/templateInterpreterGenerator_x86_32.cpp**: 32-bit x86 specifics\\n- **src/hotspot/cpu/x86/templateInterpreterGenerator_x86_64.cpp**: 64-bit x86-64 specifics\\n- **src/hotspot/cpu/x86/templateTable_x86.cpp/hpp**: X86-specific bytecode templates\\n- **src/hotspot/cpu/x86/interp_masm_x86.cpp**: Assembly macro implementation with `dispatch_base()` and `dispatch_only_normal()` methods that use the dispatch table to route to bytecode handlers\\n- **src/hotspot/cpu/x86/abstractInterpreter_x86.cpp**: Abstract interpreter specifics\\n\\n### AArch64:\\n- **src/hotspot/cpu/aarch64/templateInterpreterGenerator_aarch64.cpp**: AArch64 generator\\n- **src/hotspot/cpu/aarch64/templateTable_aarch64.cpp/hpp**: AArch64 bytecode templates\\n- **src/hotspot/cpu/aarch64/interp_masm_aarch64.cpp**: Assembly macros with dispatch implementation including `dispatch_base()` and `get_dispatch()` for loading dispatch table address\\n- **src/hotspot/cpu/aarch64/abstractInterpreter_aarch64.cpp**: Abstract interpreter specifics\\n\\n### ARM:\\n- **src/hotspot/cpu/arm/templateInterpreterGenerator_arm.cpp**: ARM generator\\n- **src/hotspot/cpu/arm/templateTable_arm.cpp/hpp**: ARM bytecode templates\\n- **src/hotspot/cpu/arm/interp_masm_arm.cpp/hpp**: Assembly macros with dispatch implementation\\n- **src/hotspot/cpu/arm/abstractInterpreter_arm.cpp**: Abstract interpreter specifics\\n\\n### PowerPC:\\n- **src/hotspot/cpu/ppc/templateInterpreterGenerator_ppc.cpp**: PowerPC generator\\n- **src/hotspot/cpu/ppc/templateTable_ppc_64.cpp/hpp**: PowerPC bytecode templates\\n- **src/hotspot/cpu/ppc/interp_masm_ppc_64.cpp**: Assembly macros with `dispatch_Lbyte_code()` for table-based dispatch\\n- **src/hotspot/cpu/ppc/abstractInterpreter_ppc.cpp**: Abstract interpreter specifics\\n\\n### RISCV:\\n- **src/hotspot/cpu/riscv/templateInterpreterGenerator_riscv.cpp**: RISCV generator\\n- **src/hotspot/cpu/riscv/templateTable_riscv.cpp/hpp**: RISCV bytecode templates\\n- **src/hotspot/cpu/riscv/interp_masm_riscv.cpp**: Assembly macros with dispatch implementation\\n- **src/hotspot/cpu/riscv/abstractInterpreter_riscv.cpp**: Abstract interpreter specifics\\n\\n### S390:\\n- **src/hotspot/cpu/s390/templateInterpreterGenerator_s390.cpp**: S390 generator\\n- **src/hotspot/cpu/s390/templateTable_s390.cpp/hpp**: S390 bytecode templates\\n- **src/hotspot/cpu/s390/interp_masm_s390.cpp**: Assembly macros with dispatch implementation\\n- **src/hotspot/cpu/s390/abstractInterpreter_s390.cpp**: Abstract interpreter specifics\\n\\n### Zero Interpreter (Portable):\\n- **src/hotspot/share/interpreter/zero/zeroInterpreterGenerator.cpp/hpp**: Zero interpreter generator\\n- **src/hotspot/cpu/zero/zeroInterpreter_zero.cpp/hpp**: Zero interpreter main loop implementation\\n- **src/hotspot/cpu/zero/bytecodeInterpreter_zero.cpp/hpp**: Bytecode-by-bytecode interpreter loop\\n\\n## How the Dispatch Loop Works\\n\\nThe dispatch loop is executed in three phases:\\n\\n1. **Dispatch Table Population**: During JVM startup, `TemplateInterpreterGenerator::set_entry_points_for_all_bytes()` iterates through all bytecode values and calls `set_entry_points()` for each to build the dispatch tables. Each bytecode template generates platform-specific code and records its entry point.\\n\\n2. **Dispatch at Runtime**: The interpreter uses the appropriate dispatch table (`_active_table`, `_normal_table`, or `_safept_table`) based on execution mode. The bytecode value is loaded and used as an index into the dispatch table, providing the address of the handler code.\\n\\n3. **Dispatch Epilog**: After each bytecode executes, `dispatch_epilog()` or `dispatch_next()` functions load the next bytecode and repeat the dispatch process.\\n\\nEach architecture implements the core dispatch mechanism through its `interp_masm_*.cpp` file, which provides architecture-specific assembly macros like `dispatch_base()` that efficiently perform the table lookup and jump to the appropriate bytecode handler.\"\n}\n",
